  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5363909b-dffa-4230-91a2-5f891c40f7d7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer16461279309372898079">Nikki Beckett could only watch as her boyfriend, Jack, sacrificed himself to save her, taking her place in the Tunnels of the Everneath for eternity — a debt that should’ve been hers. She’s living a borrowed life, and she doesn’t know what to do with the guilt.   <span id="freeText16461279309372898079" style="display:none">Nikki Beckett could only watch as her boyfriend, Jack, sacrificed himself to save her, taking her place in the Tunnels of the Everneath for eternity — a debt that should’ve been hers. She’s living a borrowed life, and she doesn’t know what to do with the guilt. And every night Jack appears in her dreams, lost and confused and wasting away.<br /><br />Desperate for answers, Nikki turns to Cole, the immortal bad boy who wants to make her his queen — and the one person least likely to help. But his heart has been touched by everything about Nikki, and he agrees to assist her in the only way he can: by taking her to the Everneath himself.<br /><br />Nikki and Cole descend into the Everneath, only to discover that their journey will be more difficult than they’d anticipated — and more deadly. But Nikki vows to stop at nothing to save Jack — even if it means making an incredible sacrifice of her own.<br /><br />In this enthralling sequel to Everneath, Brodi Ashton tests the bonds of destiny and explores the lengths we’ll go to for the ones we love.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_272039045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272039045" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272039045?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=omg-that-ending">omg-that-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-need-to-buy-this-book">i-need-to-buy-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2-am-or-later">2-am-or-later</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=didn-t-disappoint">didn-t-disappoint</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-didn-t-see-that-coming">i-didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dat-cover-yo">dat-cover-yo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-loved-it">i-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=original-and-creative">original-and-creative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-favs">2012-favs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272039045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7383044427162330364"><br/>Actual rating: 4.5 stars<br/><br/>There are exactly two types of books that I tend to gravitate towards: Dystopians and Greek myths. Both feature characters in impossible, bleak situations. Those stories are dark, deadly and often times, down right tragic, not always ending with your standardized 'happily ever after.' Hmm... I'm not exactly sure what that says about me as a person, but I digress. I think the real allure is rooting for the underdogs even when it seems like they're up against the inevitable</span>
  <span id="freeText7383044427162330364" style="display:none"><br>Actual rating: 4.5 stars<br><br>There are exactly two types of books that I tend to gravitate towards: Dystopians and Greek myths. Both feature characters in impossible, bleak situations. Those stories are dark, deadly and often times, down right tragic, not always ending with your standardized 'happily ever after.' Hmm... I'm not exactly sure what that says about me as a person, but I digress. I think the real allure is rooting for the underdogs even when it seems like they're up against the inevitable. It's the <em>spark of hope</em> in these character driven novels. The <em>passion</em> and <em>determination</em> of the main characters. The <em>dynamic relationships</em> that form as a result of these scenarios. But mostly importantly, it's the nagging thought in the back of your mind, wondering what you'd do if you were in their position, which paves the way for certain type of <em>admiration</em> for the strength in the protagonist. <em>Everbound</em> was that kind of book for me.<br><br>Immediately, after starting <em>Everbound</em> I had the sinking feeling it was going to tear at my heart. And I was right because obviously Nikki is still hurting over Jack's sacrifice with no way to save him. That is, until Cole reappears in her life and together they travel down to the Everneath to save Jack. And I should warn readers that this is not a happy novel and it does contain its fair share of teen angst, but, in my opinion, warranted. While Nikki and Cole navigate the Everneath, they rely heavily on her memories of Jack to show them the way. I was a little wary of the book containing flashbacks to help move the plot along because those types of novels don't seem to work well with me. Thankfully, I enjoyed it and I feel it helped fill the void for Jack's smallish role in this installment.<br><br>That's right. *weeps* There isn't much Jack in here. That made me really sad in the beginning, but then there was Cole, who is a completely different character for the better. Nikki is oblivious to Cole's feelings for her and at times that did annoy me. What was it going to take for her to see it? Did his love have to punch her in the face? Apparently. Yet, she failed to take much notice and that, unfortunately, led to a tragic ending... And if you're wondering, yes, there is a cliffhanger. In this case, I liked it only because I think Ashton set it up nicely even though I must now suffer more than a year to know what happens next (WHY?! *weeps* HOW SHALL I SURVIVE?).<br><br>Another thing I loved about <em>Everbound</em> was how much action was added this time around. Whereas <em>Everneath</em> moved as a slower pace and it almost felt like you could feel Nikki coming out her drugged haze, <em>Everbound</em> is the opposite with just enough action sequences, paired with bittersweet flashback memories of Nikki and Jack. But at the same time there is this layer of urgency to get to Jack before he disappears forever. So many obstacles are thrown at our characters, that I started to doubt if there would be any sort of resolution because Ashton doesn't make it easy for them. After all, this is based on a Greek myth. Remember all the tragedy, pain and suffering? Ashton really doesn't hold back and I really appreciated it.<br><br>Then there is the love triangle. And I really have to applaud Ashton for it. I know, I know. Not another dreaded love triangle. But let me tell you, I LOVE IT. Originally, I was solidly on Jack's side, but I'm finding myself more and more conflicted as this series goes on (much like I am with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/53763-unearthly" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Unearthly</em>
</a> series). There seems to be so much more to Cole than I expected. He's such a complex character and learning more about his past in <em>Everbound</em> had me questioning who the true antagonist is.  Cole says there are no heroes. But is he just resisting the person he could be or has he accepted his fate and role as a true Everliving? I am unsure. All I know is that I was throughly deceived in this book. Like, egg all over my face. Feels rain down on me. Then by the end, ultimately, I drowned in it.<br><br><a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368970ra/721581.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Usually, I have this habit where I rate books immediately after finishing the last page and this, admittedly, leads to a lot of books having inflated ratings from me. (I'm working on that.) But even after leaving <em>Everbound's</em> review waiting to be written for almost a week, I still feel this was an excellent second novel. I expected to find "Second Book Syndrome," but instead we have a story that significantly picked up the action, dived into more complex characterization and a conclusion that left me stunned. I think fans of <em>Everneath</em> will loves this and those who weren't particularly impressed with the first book will find a better novel here. There's really not much to say other than to wonder, how many children must I offer up for book three?<br><br><b>Interested in winning an ARC? Check back with us at the end of the month for our <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/2012/11/cuddlebuggerys-top-cuddles-of-2012-giveaway-hop-sign-up/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Top Cuddles of 2012 Giveaway Hop</a>. </b>(Yes, that was a bit of shameless self-promotion. I regret nothing.)<br><br> <br><br><em>ARC was provided by HarperTEEN. Thank you! As usual, no monies or favors were exchanged for a positive review. I just happened to like something all by my lonesome. Shocking, I know. </em><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things a <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br><br>----------------------<br><br>Thoughts immediately after reading:<br><br>OKAY. WHOA. That ending!! <br><br>GAHHHHHH!!!<br><br><a href="http://beta.photobucket.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368970ra/721582.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>-----------<br><br>Thoughts before reading:<br><br>Just look at that SMOKIN' cover!<br><br>Yes, DO want! Gimme!</span>

<div id="review_447317054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/447317054" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/447317054?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer447317054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13047535147552181726"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Warning: contains spoilers for the end of Everneath</b><br/><br/>I've spent most of the last hour browsing the internet and trying to find a gif that fully portrays the shock and outrage I felt at the ending of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13115995.Everbound__Everneath___2_' title='Everbound (Everneath, #2) by Brodi Ashton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Everbound</a>. Unfortunately, there appears to be nothing of that extremity currently on tumblr or photobucket. Before the last chapter, I was liking this book well enough - particularly the more action-packed scenes in the Everneath - and I was breezing along thinking "yeah yeah, this is good, that wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13047535147552181726" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Warning: contains spoilers for the end of Everneath</b><br><br>I've spent most of the last hour browsing the internet and trying to find a gif that fully portrays the shock and outrage I felt at the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13115995.Everbound__Everneath___2_" title="Everbound (Everneath, #2) by Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Everbound</a>. Unfortunately, there appears to be nothing of that extremity currently on tumblr or photobucket. Before the last chapter, I was liking this book well enough - particularly the more action-packed scenes in the Everneath - and I was breezing along thinking "yeah yeah, this is good, that was great, whatever" until Ashton hit me in the face with a great load of <b>DIDN'T SEE THAT ONE COMING</b>. This is definitely better than the first. It is an emotional rollercoaster that has you constantly reevaluating your opinions on the characters and who you want Nikki to end up with.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9413044.Everneath__Everneath___1_" title="Everneath (Everneath, #1) by Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Everneath</a> finishes where Jack has taken Nikki's place in the Everneath and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13115995.Everbound__Everneath___2_" title="Everbound (Everneath, #2) by Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Everbound</a> is all about Nikki's attempts to rescue him. With Cole's help, Nikki sets off into the Everneath, navigating the dangerous rings of water, wind and fire, in order to save Jack from his imprisonment. The Everneath uses every emotion as a weapon, plays tricks on your mind, makes doubt creep into every plan and tries to (literally) drown you in despair. In order to locate Jack, Nikki must rely on her "tether" to him which is conjured through happy memories of their relationship. Team Jack readers will probably have their hearts ripped out a few times when Nikki relives her time with him because Ashton is excellent at conveying very genuine emotions.<br><br>I think the thing I liked most that made me love this book more than the first one is that this is as much an action-packed adventure as it is an angst-filled romance. I really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9413044.Everneath__Everneath___1_" title="Everneath (Everneath, #1) by Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Everneath</a> with its new spin on Greek myths but I'm not the biggest fan of romance and cheesiness, in fact, my initial reaction to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13115995.Everbound__Everneath___2_" title="Everbound (Everneath, #2) by Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Everbound</a> was negative when Nikki was pining over Jack (understandable but still boring after a while). So when it became clear that this sequel was about way more than relationship challenges, I was delighted. Though much of it is still linked to Nikki and Jack's relationship, it is also largely about the physical and mental challenges Nikki and Cole face in the Everneath, avoiding firewalls and the zombie-like Wanderers that feed on emotion.<br><br>But most of all, the winning factor of this series for me is: complex characters. No one is simply all bad or all good, they have faults and they do bad things but the bad things are not mindless evil either. When Nikki is reminiscing about Jack in the flashbacks here, we see many different sides to his character and Ashton paints an even more vivid picture of who he is and what makes him tick. Similarly with Cole. It would have been very easy to make Cole the bad guy and leave it at that, but he has so many levels to his character and everything he does has a reason for it - whether those reasons are good enough an excuse or not depends on the reader. But, either way, this is an excellent second installment that doesn't suffer from middle book syndrome for a second.<br><br>Phew, big big yay for good sequels! Now we just have to wait a whole year for the last book...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396328ra/763791.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13047535147552181726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_276215083" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276215083" />
    <a title="Taschima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima"><img alt="Taschima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574541558p2/2435020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/276215083?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taschima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taschima" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima">Taschima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer276215083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6734201613896775461">I speculated a lot when it came to Everbound. What will Nikki do? How will she do it? Will Jack survive? Will Cole remain a romantic interest after all he did?! Will he help Nikki get Jack back? Let's just say Everneath was one of my top 2012 reads. So Everbound definitely delivered, just not quite as much as Everneath? It was good, believe me, I just liked Everneath a bit better because of well, Jack quite frankly. You get some Jack here but just in memories. He is still as cute as a button in </span>
  <span id="freeText6734201613896775461" style="display:none">I speculated a lot when it came to Everbound. What will Nikki do? How will she do it? Will Jack survive? Will Cole remain a romantic interest after all he did?! Will he help Nikki get Jack back? Let's just say Everneath was one of my top 2012 reads. So Everbound definitely delivered, just not quite as much as Everneath? It was good, believe me, I just liked Everneath a bit better because of well, Jack quite frankly. You get some Jack here but just in memories. He is still as cute as a button in memories, just not as romantically frustrated as he was in Everneath.<br><br>Things I loved about Everbound:<br><br>- The romantic angst. Sue me, sometimes, in some books, is entertaining and warranted. If Nikki were to be all happy and not sort of depressed for the story I would have screamed BULLSHIT! But she had a good happy medium of sad and determined that I admired. She didn't curl into fetus position once Jack was so rudely taken away from her (*cough* <i>Bella Swan</i> *cough*) but instead she constructed a thick wall around her heart, allowed herself to grieve while at the same time looking for a solution. You go girl!<br><br><br>- Cole. Gosh darn all Coles of this world. They are all inexplicably attractive.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380369628i/722384.jpg" width="150" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380369628i/722385.jpg" width="265" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Cole from Charmed)<br><br>Yum... Anyways. I don't picture the Cole of Everneath as this Cole but you get my point. Hotness runs in the name.<br><br>In Everbound we get to see another side of Cole. He is vulnerable, sweet, and willing to help Nikki go into the Everneath to save her boyfriend, even if it is at the cost of his own happiness. Or, is it? Gosh darn it I love what Brodi Ashton did with Cole, specially when it comes to the ending of the story. It was just, right. I have to admit, he got to me. Specially in that scene with the Siren... You have to read it for yourself. It's good.<br><br>- The Everneath is... weird. I could sort of picture it in a grand scale. Endless. I liked the barriers Ashton constructed in the Everneath, made out of water, wind, and fire. I could picture it and it looked pretty cool. My only complaint is the way they went through the barriers... may be a bit too easy? Specially the "wind" part. I mean, it was supposed to screw with your head, but they didn't seem that screwed with. I was expecting a bit more of a challenge.<br><br>- The flashbacks to how Nikki and Jack's relationship developed. Oh bless his heart! Although it kind of annoyed me how the memories were more scrambled and not a linear tale. I would have liked a more linear tale when it came to the flashbacks. But since we are sans Jack in this book I really appreciated the flashbacks.<br><br>- THE ENDING. Hell, yes! Just when you think you might be getting a happy ending... Well, you don't. Not really. I loved how it makes you re-evaluate everything you have read since the very first page. Oh Cole... you are a bastard. Just saying! A lovely bastard!<br><br><br>Things I didn't quite care for:<br><br>- The Everneath! It's just... It's so bright and sunshiny. I was picturing something more deadly a la "My Soul to Save". To me it seemed more like what a faerie kingdom would look like really. Which is why I always forget this is more loosely based on Greek Myths. To me it seems a blend of both the Faerie and Greek myth.<br><br>- I had a few questions when it came to things that happened to characters that banished in one page and return way later with no explanation. I also had questions when it came to Jack, and the surprising ending. But maybe these will be answered in the next installment so... waiting on that.<br><br>- I needed more Jack. There, I said it. Even though Cole was a nice distraction Jack is still one of a kind. Bring him back dammit!<br><br>Okay, now to speculate about the next installment... Can't wait!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6734201613896775461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_266381161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266381161" />
    <a title="Soumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi"><img alt="Soumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440767658p2/6833452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266381161?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soumi" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi">Soumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=books-i-reviewed">books-i-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=to-review">to-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266381161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1582934551280802922"><b>“I waited for you."<br/>"But it's a race. Why did you wait for me?"<br/>"I always wait for you. I'm always waiting for you.”</b><br/><br/>Tragedy in wasteland of unfathomable pain, hopeless love is a divine whine. I found this book is just as tortuously magical. A beautiful second instalment that kept the consistency of the series. It was tragic and hopeful in same line, with a grand tour to Everneath and fighting off zombie like creatures with brains. I like books of any genre but when it comes to Geek mythology, its </span>
  <span id="freeText1582934551280802922" style="display:none"><b>“I waited for you."<br />"But it's a race. Why did you wait for me?"<br />"I always wait for you. I'm always waiting for you.”</b><br /><br />Tragedy in wasteland of unfathomable pain, hopeless love is a divine whine. I found this book is just as tortuously magical. A beautiful second instalment that kept the consistency of the series. It was tragic and hopeful in same line, with a grand tour to Everneath and fighting off zombie like creatures with brains. I like books of any genre but when it comes to Geek mythology, its insanely irresistible for me. The moment I finished Everneath I felt a hidden scorch in my skin to read Everbound and this one year of waiting was simply as tortures as can get. <br /><br />Jack has sacrificed himself to save Nikki. Now it a guilt ridden Nikki wants to bring the love of her life at any cost. But her only ticket to Everneath is Cole the bad boy who is sole responsible for all the trouble Nikki faced. So they embark a journey to Everneath, deterring all the obstacles in their way. But nothing comes with a price….isn’t it? Just like Orpheus paid by his life, for Eurydice <br /><br />I loved Nikki in this book. The determination placed up to hide the feeling of loss and guilt, the swilling passion in depth of her heart and above all he dedication. She knew she was taking advantage of Cole’s love for her, using his connection to Everneath. Still her dedication to Jack just left me awed.<br /><br />Cole always tried to be the bad guy. He kept convincing Nikki that he was no hero, but in the end he helped her, know it might endanger his own existence. I liked how his character has been portrayed, complex yet sympathetic. But also, there were portions of his minds in depth of danger that were off limits to anyone, even to Nikki. Yet, with all his flaws, I loved Cole.<br /><br /><b>Jack, dude, do i know ya?</b> I have nothing much to say about Jack. His character was overshadowed by Cole. Only that he was holding on Nikki’s love, the only hope of his survival. However he mostly appeared in Nikki’s flashbacks and dreams. There not much Jack in this sequel but I hope to see him in action soon.<br /><br />Everbound was written in a very clear language and in such a touching way. Every chapter was equally exciting. The ending was not a cliff-hanger like the first book, it was rather a comedy than a tragedy. <br />The series is not you usual re-imagining of Persephone and Hades myths, it's much more different and original.<br /><br />Overall, if you have already read Everbound, you’ll be changed for a crime if you don’t read Everbound. And if you haven’t yet read Everneath, you must hurry to buy it. Trust me the series is worth reading. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1582934551280802922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6590861503054291849" style="display:none">I propose we begin a foundation. Survivors of the Everneath Series Anonymous. Because this book seriously gave me ALL the feels:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401339i/778897.jpg" alt="Feels. She has to make it through three mazes, avoid zombie-like wanderers, the Queen of the Everneath and the Shades or she and Jack are going to die.<br><br>And can I just say: GOD THIS BOOK! WHY?! How could you give us such an ending – AGAIN!?<br><br>I read the last page of this book with the colour draining from my face, shaking my head and going, “No! No! Noooooo! She got me again!” I mean, there’s just so mean you can be to your readers before they’re justified in kidnapping you and forcing you to hand over any and all sequels!<br><br>Nikki continues to improve as a character – taking leaps and bounds as a stronger, more amazing character. She is not afraid to hit back at life and she doesn’t hesitate to kick butt when it needs kicking. However, the scene stealer is most definitely Cole who will charm the pants off you, then charm your pants, then steal your pants. Because that boy is evil and if I were to ever translate myself into a fictional world in order to meet him then I’d probably slap him, kiss him and then slap him again for good measure.<br><br>Seriously, this sequel was amazing and has set the bar very high for the third book in the Everneath series which I absolutely need. <div id="review_253143277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253143277" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253143277?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=heroes-i-adore">heroes-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=oh-my-god-marry-me">oh-my-god-marry-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=2013-faves">2013-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253143277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2518524070527934127">This review is also available over at <a href='http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-everbound-by-brodi-ashton.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog.</a><br/><br/>________________________<br/><br/>This. Book. Gave. Me. <i>Everything</i>.<br/><br/>Right off the bat, when I saw a map of the Everneath at the beginning of the book, I was freaking out. After the emotional, character-based first book, I had always hoped that its sequel would take us deep into the Everneath, with lots more action. And in the end that was what this book did.<br/><br/>I love Brodi Ashton for that, because she made the perfect balance. The first book focused mostly on the </span>
  <span id="freeText2518524070527934127" style="display:none">This review is also available over at <a href="http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-everbound-by-brodi-ashton.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog.</a><br /><br />________________________<br /><br />This. Book. Gave. Me. <i>Everything</i>.<br /><br />Right off the bat, when I saw a map of the Everneath at the beginning of the book, I was freaking out. After the emotional, character-based first book, I had always hoped that its sequel would take us deep into the Everneath, with lots more action. And in the end that was what this book did.<br /><br />I love Brodi Ashton for that, because she made the perfect balance. The first book focused mostly on the characters, and had a contemporary-ish feel to it. And I applaud her for making this one a lot more action-y, yet still have that emotion that made me love the first book so much.<br /><br />This series also has a love triangle that I really like. I love that Nikki is completely devoted to Jack, and despite Cole's hotness and protectiveness toward her, she doesn't go and fall for him in a snap, like I'm pretty sure most heroines would do. In fact, Nikki still has trouble fully trusting Cole. Later on we find out that that's for a good reason, but I won't spoil anything, don't worry~<br /><br />Another thing I love is that both guys haven't given up on Nikki. We all know most YA heroes would end up jumping to the next vagina in sight when they lose the heroine. Cole is always waiting for that moment where Nikki could be all his, even though he knows that may never happen. My heart kind of broke for him in a few of the scenes, because he genuinely does love Nikki. Nikki doesn't lead him on or anything, though, which I think is smart. Cause if she did . . . girl, bye.<br /><br />By the way, we <i>finally</i> get some backstory from Cole! Although, once again, it's very shortened. I have a feeling that Ms. Brodi Ashton here is doing this on purpose to make Cole all mysterious and stuff. My problem with him still remains the same thing that I discussed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/427458639" rel="nofollow noopener">my <i>Neverfall</i> review</a>, that it's hard for me to fully believe he's immortal. Besides that, though, I love him.<br /><br />And Jack . . . oh, Jack. It should be a crime how perfect he is. And by perfect I don't mean in the chiseled Greek god kinda way like in most paranormal YA books, because he's not only perfect looks-wise, but he's so damn <i>sweet</i>! Gah, he's seriously every girl's dream, and I can see why Nikki would rather cut her arm off than give up on him. Because really, there's no topping Jack Caputo.<br /><br />But most of all, the highlight of this book to me is the Everneath, because I've been dying to explore it from the very beginning. I love how it was designed. We get to see almost every part of the Everneath, and even meet the queen! Nearing the end there's a twist involving her that I really liked.<br /><br />And then there was that one final twist in the final chapter, and I'm like, "Oh. Shit." I absolutely cannot wait for the third book, because I really have no idea what to expect from it. Like, really. I knew what to expect from this book because it was pretty clear that it was going to be about Nikki trying to save Jack. But for the third book, I really don't know what to expect, and that makes me both excited and frustrated.<br /><br />I really, really love this series. And I'm pretty sure waiting for the next book is gonna kill me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2518524070527934127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_515081977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/515081977" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/515081977?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515081977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer743911179823629594">With <i>Everbound</i>, I get the exact same feeling as I had with its predecessor, <i>Everneath</i>. I like Brodi Ashton’s unique spin on Greek mythology, particularly the myth of Hades and Persephone, but for me, it’s just missing something. I guess beyond the premise I just don’t see how the execution of this series stands out from every other paranormal romance featuring a girl, two guys, and a supernatural plot involving the three I’ve ever read, so while the paranormal hook is fairly interesting, the res</span>
  <span id="freeText743911179823629594" style="display:none">With <i>Everbound</i>, I get the exact same feeling as I had with its predecessor, <i>Everneath</i>. I like Brodi Ashton’s unique spin on Greek mythology, particularly the myth of Hades and Persephone, but for me, it’s just missing something. I guess beyond the premise I just don’t see how the execution of this series stands out from every other paranormal romance featuring a girl, two guys, and a supernatural plot involving the three I’ve ever read, so while the paranormal hook is fairly interesting, the rest of this feels like just another angst filled blatant play for emotions that leaves me feeling nothing.<br /><br />I’m assuming a big part of the appeal is supposed to be Nikki’s reaction to Jack’s sacrifice that was the cliffhanger of <i>Everneath</i>. And it’s supposed to be really romantic the way Nikki ‘saves’ Jack by connecting with him through her dreams like he did for her. Maybe it is, but the only thing the setup does for me is continuously remind me of a song I’ve been trying to forget since 1997:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Every night in my dreams, I see you, I feel you, that is how I know you go on…</i>
</blockquote><br />Yeah, with Jack (see? see?) now in the Tunnels, the only way Nikki knows he’s alive is when he visits her in her dreams.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Far across the distance, and spaces between us, you have come to show you go on…</i>
</blockquote><br />Again, he’s in the Tunnels, she’s stuck in our surface world. There are spaces between them. Her heart goes on as long as she knows he alive...<br /><br />Anyway, I could go on with line by line comparisons between <i>Everbound</i> and <i>My Heart Will Go On</i>, but I don’t want to crib this entire review from Celine Dion. I guess what I’m trying to say is that the relationship between Nikki and Jack is supposed to be romantic and sad and heartbreaking and I’m supposed to feel for Nikki as she goes on this epic quest to save her epic love, but while I liked how Ashton develops Jack’s character and Jack and Nikki’s relationship using some very cleverly incorporated flashbacks, maybe I’m just too jaded or too much of a guy but the whole thing never goes beyond the trite and manufactured and forced stage of <i>Titanic</i> style lameness for me. I mean, I get why Nikki loves Jack and wants to save him, but between the way Nikki’s written, a mix of desperation – to explain why she agrees to become Cole’s forfeit in the first place - and determination - since she’s ultimately responsible for what happens to Jack, and the borderline melodramatic responses to her and Jack’s disappearances from Jack’s mother and her father, I don’t know, I just see how intentionally angsty everything is and really didn’t care for Nikki or for Jack or for Nikki's whole quest to save Jack. And when I’m disinterested and uncaring, well, I guess I’m missing the appeal of the series? <br /><br />At this point, I’m pretty much only reading for the mythology and for Cole. I had my guesses about the Everneath and how it worked from the first book, and I’m glad Ashton fleshes out the Everneath way beyond the vague mentions before, although Nikki’s journey through the Everneath to rescue Jack didn’t really stand out from other quests through mythical lands I’ve seen before - well, except for the cavern of hands, that was really good. Ashton’s twists on the original myths, as always, are really inspired and one of the few bright spots of the series; she’s made enough changes that I know how the originals go and my initial reaction’s always ‘that’s not how it is at all!’ but I always end up seeing how the changes work in the grander scheme of the overall mythology. Cole of course is the one well written character is a sea of mediocrity and really the only reason why I’m still reading this - it’s rare to find a truly conflicted character with shades of gray who does evil things not just because but with actual reasons behind them. Still, why he keeps associating with Nikki who desperately needs a new angle to her existence besides just ‘Jack! Jack!’ is beyond me.<br /><br />Basically, if it wasn’t for Cole and his ulterior motives, I probably would’ve given up on this series some time ago. Even still, I’m mostly barely tolerating Nikki and Jack just to see what Cole’ll do next. Not a ringing endorsement, I know.</span>
  <a data-text-id="743911179823629594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_976982469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/976982469" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/976982469?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer976982469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16827218779813462357"><b> 5 Ever Yours stars! </b><br/><br/>Everbound begins a couple of weeks after the events of Everneath. After her boyfriend Jack sacrifices himself and is sent into the tunnels of the everneath, Nikki makes it her mission to rescue Jack from what should have been her fate. To do this, Nikki must go to the everneath, and she needs the help of Cole, the everling who instigated this whole mess. Surprisingly, Cole is willing to help Nikki, and both of them set off on a dangerous journey to reunite Nikki with her los</span>
  <span id="freeText16827218779813462357" style="display:none"><b> 5 Ever Yours stars! </b><br /><br />Everbound begins a couple of weeks after the events of Everneath. After her boyfriend Jack sacrifices himself and is sent into the tunnels of the everneath, Nikki makes it her mission to rescue Jack from what should have been her fate. To do this, Nikki must go to the everneath, and she needs the help of Cole, the everling who instigated this whole mess. Surprisingly, Cole is willing to help Nikki, and both of them set off on a dangerous journey to reunite Nikki with her lost love. Along the way Nikki recounts stories of her and Jack, which helps form a tether in the everneath which will lead her to Jack.<br /><br />I admired Nikki's determination in this book. Where she had been sort of a weakling in the first book, she developed into a fighter in Everbound. She fought many difficult obstacles to get to Jack, and suceeded where many other people would have given up.<br /><br /><b> <i> "I was not losing Jack. I would not lose him." </i> </b><br /><br />I loved how the author began to "humanize" Cole in this book. In the last book he seemed to be strictly The Bad Guy, but in Everbound I found myself wanting to know more about him. As a reader, his love for Nikki becomes more prevalent and believable in this addition.<br /><br /><b> <i> "It's not love. It's a need. He needs me because he thinks I can become the next queen. He doesn't love me."<br />"You really can't see it, can you?"<br />"See what?"<br />"He has a tether too. And it points right at you." </i> </b><br /><br />I thought the love triangle was very well done. I am usually a fan of the underdog, which in this case would mean Cole. Despite the character development of him and the lack of Jack's presence on page, I found myself rooting for Jack instead of Cole. Like, I am a t-shirt wearing fan of #TeamJack. I think this is because Jack suffered through so much in book one of Nikki being gone (and it being Cole's fault), and then his self sacrifice. His actions just makes him a character you have to root for. Don't get me wrong, Cole is all kinds of interesting. I just don't want him to get the girl.<br /><br />And that ending? Boy am I glad I waited to read this series until all of them were published. Mini-cliffhanger!!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16827218779813462357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3327641515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText8385135686326847285" style="display:none">First thing, I want to appreciate the map on the very beginning of the book.<br />It is such a beautiful map, I didn't even realize it was a map at the first glance. I tought what I saw were some symbols (from the ring).<br /><br />This was good second book in the series. We got to see Everneath and the writer did a decent job in the world building.<br /><br />As for characters, <b>I really liked Nikki's development</b>. She is full of anger that makes her stronger. I really liked that about her. Her anger makes her a fighter, keeps her going. She knows what she wants and she's ready to fight and do whatever it takes to reach her goal.<br /><br />I don't want to spoil anyone but I will say that one character had let me down big time.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cole, you little prick!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'll end this (let's call it) review here and I'm off to read <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13626692.Evertrue__Everneath___3_" title="Evertrue (Everneath, #3) by Brodi Ashton" rel="nofollow noopener">Evertrue</a>.<br /><br />Note: <i>I don't want to be cruel but I really hope a little bastard will die in the next book.</i><br /><br /><b>Right after finishing the book: </b><br /><br />This book (or I should say one specific character) made me angry. It's so bad that my adrenaline got high, and now I know I won't fall into sleep any time soon.</span>

<div id="review_370823367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/370823367" />
    <a title="Joan{missing the vampire bunny slippers!}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5116644-joan-missing-the-vampire-bunny-slippers"><img alt="Joan{missing the vampire bunny slippers!}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447247293p2/5116644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/370823367?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joan{missing the vampire bunny slippers!}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joan{missing the vampire bunny slippers!}" href="/user/show/5116644-joan-missing-the-vampire-bunny-slippers">Joan{missing the vampire bunny slippers!}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116644-joan-missing-the-vampire-bunny-slippers?shelf=ebooks-i-have">ebooks-i-have</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer370823367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer89951359324516041">SPOILER ALERT!<br/><br/> I don't mean to leak any big spoilers, but since I have some strong feelings about this ending I can't help, but spoil a bit. Or a lot. Whatever... :P<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374435ra/728459.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> Cole you sneaky, manipulative bastard! :D<br/> Now that was a twist!<br/> Not that I didn't expect it to happen at some point I just thought it would be on the next book and that it would happen after she agreed... But, damn! He really blindsided me! Which is mainly the reason why my 3.5 stars became 4 and not 3!<br/><br/> I know I 've said it many tim</span>
  <span id="freeText89951359324516041" style="display:none">SPOILER ALERT!<br><br> I don't mean to leak any big spoilers, but since I have some strong feelings about this ending I can't help, but spoil a bit. Or a lot. Whatever... :P<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374435ra/728459.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> Cole you sneaky, manipulative bastard! :D<br> Now that was a twist!<br> Not that I didn't expect it to happen at some point I just thought it would be on the next book and that it would happen after she agreed... But, damn! He really blindsided me! Which is mainly the reason why my 3.5 stars became 4 and not 3!<br><br> I know I 've said it many times so far, but wow!! Even if I suspected the end I would <b>never</b> suspect that it would be deliberate and calculated like that! <br> When I started this I wasn't sure I could go through with it, since after the long period of time between the two releases I had disconnected myself from the characters. And that was true until they went into Everneath! <br> I was a little annoyed by Nikki's constant mental ranting, but maybe she should be even more paranoid after all. She is not my favorite character and it must be a huge complement to the author's writing, because even though I am not hooked by any of the characters and I can't personally relate to them at all, I still read these books in a matter of a few days! And I ultimately enjoyed both of them. <br> I was right that having Max along would be more fun! The way he interacts with Cole and to see him probing him and making him reveal bits and peaces of himself was priceless.<br> Jack was very absent from this book aside from his appearances in Nikki's dreams and memories. I wasn't all that bothered by the fact, but I still like him well enough.<br> Cole was a roller-coaster ride for me! I never like him at first and then I do and then I don't, etc... He has a different kind of charm. He's not <i>bad</i>, at least not to Nikki, because we've seen him kill before,he is manipulative and he doesn't hesitate to use anyone in order to make ends meet. He more than proved that here! I was aghast when I saw him admit to everything! I was trying sooo hard to make up excuses for him that hearing him just confess and wait to face the music brought me to such an abrupt halt my head was spinning! <br> I start the book thinking "Ok this will be boring and I will be disappointed!". Then when I start getting awfully tired of just hearing Nikki sniveling, things start to take off. They get into Everneath and there is more Cole and Max and things are finally picking up. And then halfway through the book without even realizing what's happening I'm half-rooting for Cole... Which is totally absurd 'cause I don't even like the guy all that much. And then I learn he was a Viking and I get all excited - don't ask me why it's a weird thing that it somehow clicked right for me... So when he jumps with her and he's all supportive even though I am reluctant and I don't trust him completely I start falling for it. And that's when he kicks her in the stomach! Don't even ask! But I still hope that it was to protect her or something... And when Jack appears I think "Yeah! He's not all bad after all!" <br><br>And then comes the real kicker and I'm left like this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/625807.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ok he never was a good guy, but he has some patience and he must be one of the most determined characters I've <i>
  <b>ever</b>
</i> read about and that's saying something!<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="89951359324516041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_366246958" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/366246958" />
    <a title="Sophia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4769245-sophia"><img alt="Sophia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598222002p2/4769245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/366246958?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/4769245-sophia">Sophia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer366246958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13894900315703536686">Rating: 1<br/>Writing: 1<br/>Plot: 2<br/>Characters: 1<br/><br/>Sequel to Everneath.<br/><br/>Theme: "Myths"<br/><br/>Worth the buy? .......<br/><br/>Nikki Beckett could only watch as her boyfriend, Jack, sacrificed himself to save her, taking her place in the Tunnels of the Everneath for eternity — a debt that should’ve been hers. She’s living a borrowed life, and she doesn’t know what to do with the guilt. And every night Jack appears in her dreams, lost and confused and wasting away.<br/><br/>Desperate for answers, Nikki turns to Cole, the immortal bad boy</span>
  <span id="freeText13894900315703536686" style="display:none">Rating: 1<br />Writing: 1<br />Plot: 2<br />Characters: 1<br /><br />Sequel to Everneath.<br /><br />Theme: "Myths"<br /><br />Worth the buy? .......<br /><br />Nikki Beckett could only watch as her boyfriend, Jack, sacrificed himself to save her, taking her place in the Tunnels of the Everneath for eternity — a debt that should’ve been hers. She’s living a borrowed life, and she doesn’t know what to do with the guilt. And every night Jack appears in her dreams, lost and confused and wasting away.<br /><br />Desperate for answers, Nikki turns to Cole, the immortal bad boy who wants to make her his queen — and the one person least likely to help. But his heart has been touched by everything about Nikki, and he agrees to assist her in the only way he can: by taking her to the Everneath himself.<br /><br />Nikki and Cole descend into the Everneath, only to discover that their journey will be more difficult than they’d anticipated — and more deadly. But Nikki vows to stop at nothing to save Jack — even if it means making an incredible sacrifice of her own.<br /><br />In this enthralling sequel to Everneath, Brodi Ashton tests the bonds of destiny and explores the lengths we’ll go to for the ones we love.<br /><br />This book was positively atrocious. I'm sorry, but I absolutely hated this book! I mean, I hated the first book as well. I only read it because someone said it was a re-telling of the Persephone myth. Last time I checked, no one fed on Persephone's soul. Actually, the Persephone myth was meant to explain the seasons. To me, being in love with mythology, it seems like this author did no research on mythology. If she did, she didn't incorporate it at all. In the book, it is said that mythology holds "some truths", but when they actually talk about mythology, some of the time they don't even mention names. It was like she was deliberately trying to say, 'Hey! I did research!' but then she would only add half of the story, like she skimmed through the myths.<br /><br />I hate Nikki. I absolutely despise her and for most of the book, I hoped the Everneath would swallow her. First of all, I hate how people call her Becks. I didn't remember this from the first book, so I was completely confused. If a character has a nickname, it should be a part of her actual first name. Like Nik was a fine nickname! But that was just a tiny problem I had. The biggest problem I had with Nikki was that she is inexcusably stupid. I like how characters don't know everything and things don't always work out for them, but in the book she decided she needed Cole. So when he finally sees her again, she's a jerk to him. She has no respect for him and hates him. Fine. But if you need a person, at least try to be nice or pretend to be. She wasn't even threatening him. She completely forgot about her goal to get her boyfriend back because she hated Cole. Then, she rips out his hair, runs away and eats it. I thought that was the creepiest thing. I know she had a reason for doing that, but still.<br /><br />I also hate Nikki because the whole book, she throws herself a pity party. She's whiny and annoying, and in the beginning, she said she needed to save Jack but she was running out of time. She needed Cole's help, but he was travelling. So she was waiting for him to come back, but really! If something is that urgent, she should have found him. It wouldn't have been hard; she just needed to look up where the band was playing. And Nikki should also stop worrying about her sob-story past. She was a stupid Mary Sue and I could completely see her getting Stockholm syndrome. Her and Jack aren't even a good couple! He's unrealistic, Cole is a stereotype and Nikki can't stop complaining about her life. She's the epitome of teen-angst.<br /><br />Other than the fact that I hate the main character with passion, the book isn't well written at all. There are too many fragments for drama. "More like studying. Every myth I could get my hands on." Technically, this is proper grammar, but it's awkward. More like studying every myth I could get my hands on is a better sentence, whereas the first 'sentences' are just two separated dependent clauses. There's also un-needed detail, like a paragraph describing bacon. There were no transitions and I think some scenes were added in to make Nikki's life more tragic. Boo hoo. There are information dumps, horrible characters and poor grammar....so yeah, I really didn't like this book. If you want to read a real Persephone myth, read Abandon by Meg Cabot or the Goddess Test by Aimee Carter. They aren't my favorite, but they're better than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13894900315703536686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Honestly, I don't know how Cole dealt with Nikki. Her memories of Jack integrated into the story were cute at first, but then it turned into plain corny. Corny to the point where it got</span>
  <span id="freeText4675046965975641397" style="display:none">I was <i>so</i> close to giving this book 2 stars, but just because Cole is awesome, I shall give it 3.<br><br>MY FACE WHEN I READ THE SYNOPSIS:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402894i/783490.jpg" width="100" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>MY FACE POST-READING THE BOOK:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380402894i/783491.jpg" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No. Just, no. I did not like this book. Period. I think its because I pretty much despised Nikki, but I just wasn't feeling it for this book.<br><br>You know what? Honestly, I don't know how Cole dealt with Nikki. Her memories of Jack integrated into the story were cute at first, but then it turned into plain corny. Corny to the point where it got really agitating.<br><br>Her obsession with Jack was a little creepy. Ya, he got sucked into the Underworld or wherever the hell he went, but <i>come on</i>. I get so angry when a female protagonist is unable to function without her boyfriend. They don't care about their family or their friends, they just become detached from everything. The only "friend" she had was that lady that was a part of the Daughters of Persephone thing (I forgot her name), and that was only out of her selfishness and desperation to find Jack. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[AKA Mr. Perfect <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And that "Hands" scene at the end. That was unbelievably stupid. Was that supposed to be the "climax"? Because all it did was make me yawn from boredom and its lame-ness.<br><br>That ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[freaking cliffhanger <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> just baffled me. You know how an author usually drops little hints throughout the story, otherwise known as foreshadowing? Well, this author basically shoved the information at us at the last minute. Which, naturally, angered me and confused me at the same time.<br><br>I don't like the way Nikki views Cole. She didn't seem grateful at all that he was going with her to the Everneath on a dangerous journey. She acted like he was <i>obligated</i> to do so. I mean, at least have the manners to say "Thanks" for all the crap she put him through.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Its not like she <i>knew</i> he was going to betray her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And another thing. She never considers things from his perspective. She automatically assumes he is a "bad guy". Have some empathy, girl. <br><br>I feel like there wasn't enough dialogue between the charcters. Yes, there was dialogue between Cole and Nikki and Nikki and Will, but that's about it. She did not interact with anyone else, and if she did, it was very minimal. As a result of this, we learned very little about the secondary characters- that I thought were pretty important. Like Ashe and Max, for example.<br><br>The fact that I finished this book in a day and that the author managed to keep me reading is a good sign, which is why I gave this book 3 stars. But, Nikki was just way too annoying and selfish, and everything about her was unlikable. <br><br>Cole is a different story- I am almost positive that he is the reason why I kept reading. <br><br>Excuse me while I continuously ponder why Cole wants to spend all eternity with this unbearable character. Cole, you can do better than that. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_290534938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290534938" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290534938?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290534938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15151439089507550897">Another awesome series! I read Everneath on a whim. It was a debut novel, I wasn’t sure what to expect but it sounded like something that I would enjoy. And I am SO GLAD that I did! And while I loved Everneath, Everbound was a-freaking-mazing! It’s my favorite of the two.<br/><br/>Ashton does an excellent job in book one, setting up this world and these characters. And she does an even more wonderful expanding on that in book two. We are exposed to the Everneath in a way I never thought possible, it was c</span>
  <span id="freeText15151439089507550897" style="display:none">Another awesome series! I read Everneath on a whim. It was a debut novel, I wasn’t sure what to expect but it sounded like something that I would enjoy. And I am SO GLAD that I did! And while I loved Everneath, Everbound was a-freaking-mazing! It’s my favorite of the two.<br /><br />Ashton does an excellent job in book one, setting up this world and these characters. And she does an even more wonderful expanding on that in book two. We are exposed to the Everneath in a way I never thought possible, it was crazy! I love Ashton’s references to Greek Mythology, even the ones that I totally overlooked, thanks to Kelly for pointing that one out!<br /><br />This next bit could be a bit spoilery so please skip to the next paragraph if you haven’t read book one. One thing that I missed in this installment was Jack. He really grew on me in book one, and it killed me that he sacrificed himself for Nikki and ended up in the tunnels! So since he’s stuck down there, we don’t really get to see much of him at all. Sad<br /><br />Okay, it’s safe to read again! I must have a thing for bad boys because, oh how I felt for Cole! All I wanted to do was hug him and tell him that Nikki really does love him and then slap Nikki and tell her to forget about Jack! Even though I loved Jack in book one! I think perhaps it was because of his absence. It was Cole time in Everbound. Cole all the time!<br /><br />And then the ending. I don’t even know what to say. I died. I died a little bit inside. I totally did not see any of that coming. BLINDSIDED! I couldn’t believe it! But it was so EPIC at the same time. I commend Ashton, she totally snuck all that by me.<br /><br />I love this story, and I can’t WAIT for more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15151439089507550897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
